O sons, I have finished this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, because of your faith in me, because of your exposure, and because of your declarations, so I have undertaken to complete this treatise for you, which is a part of my art, that is to say, surgery.</end_of_turn>
For surgery is very rare in our land and in our time, so that the science of it is almost lost; and its witnesses are few; and it remains only with some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which alter the most and aggravate those errors and hesitation which were in them until understanding of them is clarified and their power and art is increased.</end_of_turn
And I believe that I have composed this treatise in such a way that it follows the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and that it should be added to the forms of the instruments of cautery and other instruments of the work as well as for the addition of the declaration, and for preparation, which is necessary.</end_of_turn
The greatest cause for which a good craftsman is not found in our time in this art is that the art of medicine is long, and that it embraces many actors who must exercise themselves in the science of anatomy, since Gualius knew the movements of the limbs and the shapes of these, and the connection and separation of these; and the knowledge of bones, nerves and veins, and the number of these, and their colors; and of the pulse veins and the quietness of these, and the places of their sensation.</end_of_turn
And thus says Hippocrates that in my name is more, in the small work, and especially in the art of the hand.</end_of_turn>
And as we said at the beginning of this book, whoever is not learned in anatomy is not worthy of the name of a physician, because many have perished by the hands of those who have erred in this science. Indeed, I have seen many who have been trained in this science and have abandoned it.</end_of_turn
For I have seen a foolish and ignorant physician who, having incised an abscess of scrofula in the groin of a woman, has inciscated several arteries of the groin so that great blood flowed into her, and the woman died between her thighs.</end_of_turn
And I have seen another physician who, because he thought that a tumor had grown in a man who was in his prime, extracted that tumor with a piece of the bladder, and the man died on the third day.</end_of_turn
And I have already told you that I will speak of these things, and I have seen that because of the greatness of the tumor and the condition of the patient, he knew that he would die.</end_of_turn
And I have seen another physician who took a fee from a duke from our land for surgery, and he was indebted to a black slave who was his servant; and the physician, in his ignorance, extracted the fracture, with sponges and cloths, with great tension, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then I will show you according to your desires, and I will relieve you, and I will tell you to leave for a few days and command you to rest; and thus this matter was settled until the wound came out spontaneously, and the patient perished.</end_of_turn>
And I went to him and I showed him that the liament should be removed, and peace and joy appeared on his face, so that he forgot his pains.</end_of_turn
And indeed corruption had already been confirmed in the limb, for it was not able to restrain that, and it did not cease to spread corruption in the limb until the patient perished.</end_of_turn>
And I have seen another physician who performed an operation on a cancerous tumor, and made an ulcer nearby for several days, until the tumor grew bigger than it had before.</end_of_turn
The cause of this is that cancer is pure melancholic humor, and that it does not suffice for it to be overcome by all the forces of the will, but that it should be overcome in every limb in which the patient suffers from it.</end_of_turn
And for this reason, sons, it is necessary for you that the art of surgery be divided into two parts: that is, in surgery in which there is associated health, and in surgery in which there is peril in the greatest precautions.</end_of_turn
And I have already spoken of this in all this book in the place where I mentioned surgery in which there is error and fear; for it is necessary for you to guard against this and to leave that behind, so that the fools do not think that they can speak and despise you.</end_of_turn
Therefore take up the sacred arms in the request of God, and the sacred sick in the mercy and protection of God.
And use the best way through God's grace to preserve health and praiseworthy success, and lay aside the terrible diseases of difficult healing, and rest the sacred arms from those which make you fear, so that you may rejoice in your faith and in your name, for it is remaining for your glory, both here and hereafter with the holy ones.</end_of_turn>
Indeed, I have already spoken in several of your monasteries.</end_of_turn> “No cure any disease badly, for thus no will many doctors be named.”</end_of_turn
And I have already finished this book according to three chapters.</end_of_turn>
Begin the division of the book, and first of the first part.</end_of_turn The first chapter ordered of the head downwards, concerning the forms of instruments and the utensils of cautery, and what is necessary for the operation.</end_of_turn
The division of the second part.</end_of_turn The second chapter, concerning swelling and perforation, and windings, and ulcers, and the extraction of arrows and similar things, all classified and ordered concerning the forms of instruments.</end_of_turn
The third chapter, concerning restoration and dislocation, and care of twists and similar things; classified and ordered from the head downwards, and concerning the forms of instruments.</end_of_turn
Since I have said what is the quality of the instruments of that cautery and their documents, and in what completion it is prohibited to cauterize.</end>
Therefore I say that the speech concerning the quality of the cautery instruments and their documents is a long and profound speech, subtle for science, and a secret hidden; and that many learned men have spoken of it, and they disagree with each other, and to me it seems that a little of their speeches suffices, fearing a prolongation.</end>
Therefore I say that cautery conforms to all universal completion except for two completions, which are caudal completions of its matter.</end
In the caudal and dry completion with its matter, disagreement arises; for some say that cautery is useful for that, while others say the opposite, that cautery is not convenient in diseases of the same kind as its quality and dryness, for the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that the disease be cold and dry with what is cauterized and dry to be healed.</end
And I say that whoever says the opposite, that for cautery is useful in every cold and dry disease that is seen in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of a man with the humidity of the air to the completion of the fire, you find the body of a man cold.
And I say concerning this speech that I have already experienced it several times in my practice.</end
However, I do not say that because of this everything concerning that which has already been exposed and exercised in the chapter of cautery after practice, and to know the diversity of the men and the situation of diseases in their bodies, and the causes of these, and their accidents, and the space of time of these.</end
However, in other completions, this is not your fear, and especially in cold and wet diseases, for already all doctors agree on these, and they do not disagree concerning the use of cautery in these.</end
And know, children, that from the secret of healing by cautery with fire and of the goodness of it, is about cautery with acute medicine, for the fire is simple, the action of which reaches only the member that is cauterized and does not notice the other member with it adjusted except for a small document.</end
For the action of acute medicine reaches only that in the limb from which it is administered, and it makes it come into the diseased limb of difficult healing and makes it go away.</end<end_turn>
For the fire, by its subtlety and substance, does not do anything but what is already known to us by experience and by the length of our service in the study of the truth of causes; and for this reason I am excused from the length of this speech, for it is not written in this book for you the secret of the fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and the expulsion of the disease by which it is expelled.
Indeed, master, the best time for cautery and rest is in the earlier days of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, so that its document for the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which makes the cautery hurtful, especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, which do not suffer from delay, for fear of those who come late, which is greater than a small document entering at the time.</end_of_turn>
And I do not say that we must not cut in other cases, or, master, those who do not esteem but the vulgar people and fools among the doctors, so it is that for that disease which is cured by cautery, it is not ridiculous at all times, and rest that consequence.</end_of_turn>
And the cause is not thus that they say because it is cut, for cautery is nothing but in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humors which are the cause of these pains.</end_of_turn
However, excessive cautery surpasses medicine by the will of its value and the virtue of its operation and greatness of the patient.</end_of_turn>
And it is possible that the disease will return at any hour of the time, according to the complexion of the disease and the location of the disease, and the virtue of the things which are prepared in the body from the accumulation of humors in it, and that which is obtained by them in their acquisition in food and drinks and the like of those causes; but when the disease in which cautery is administered is a subtle disease in a limb with few superfluities and humors, just as if it were cautery for pain and like that, it is possible that in them the said pain will not return, even if it is made small.</end_of_turn>
And it may be said vulgarly that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a subtle art, not to those who understand it, for they grow that it is not a cure that makes use of medicine or any other cause except cautery.</end_of_turn
And the cause is contrary to that; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is true only when they administer the methods of care in certain diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and at the end of the cause they administer manuevers of cautery, and take advantage of that.</end_of_turn And the hour has passed sixteen that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which the vulgar people and the fools of the doctors have.</end_of_turn
And I say to them the old men that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and I do not say anything but for the equality of the gold and the limitation of its substance.</end_of_turn
And I say that the place of cautery does not make it bad, as it is not absolutely true, for I have already seen that it does not do anything but in cases where the others do not work, and that cautery with that is good and better than with iron, just as they say; however, when you make cautery with fire from gold, it is not your business to declare, for it is ignited according to the quantity you wish for the roughness of the gold, and prepare to receive cold; and if you adjust over it the fire will consume the gold for the fire, and if there are some plates in the fire so that the craftsman cuts for the occupation of that.</end_of_turn
And for this reason it is useful to make cautery with iron, we must put it more lightly and more cautiously to the rectification of the operation.</end_of_turn
And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those who are coming after me to do the same concerning the feet, so that I may relieve those who ask me what they want of me.</end_of_turn
First chapter.</end_of_turn>
This cauterization confers cold and humidity upon the accidental cause of which it is useful, so it is the cause of soda and multiple flows of rheumatic flux, applied to the cortex, from the head to the limbs and the joints fluent, and multiple of sleep, and toothache and gut pain, and universally of all diseases that come from cold, even as paralysis, sopor and apoplexy, and it is similar in these diseases.</end_of_turn
The way of this cauterization is as follows: first command the patient to evacuate with laxatives for three or four nights, according as you exceed the virtue of the disease and the age of it and its custom.</end_of_turn
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and do that between his thighs on a fallen bench and place his hands on his feet.</end_of_turn
And keep your wrist close to the thumb, over the bridge of the nose between the eyebrows. Moreover, when the doctor suspects the location of the pain, he should touch it and with a pointed cautery he should burn a little olive oil of the shape of that:
Then he should place it over the painful area, holding it firmly so that the hand does not slip away, and you should gradually tighten it
Then lift your hand lightly and support the area, and if you see already some quantity of the head of the bone uncovered, thus as much as the quantity of barley of errors, then raise your hand again, and if it has not returned, do the same with the other hand, until it is seen from the bone that you have said.
And take a little salt and dissolve it on the area and keep it there for three days.
And keep it covered in oil at the border and keep it there until the burn of the fire is healed And take care of the area with four medicines until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
And I say that when the wound remains open, so much honey should be given to the patient, because it is better and more helpful.</start_of_turn>
I say to you that the bone should be cauterized until the bone itself, and that it should be held cauterized until all the parts of the substance of the bone have healed.</start_of_turn>
And keep it moist that which is adjacent to the bone, and keep it cured.</start_of_turn
And I say that it should be cauterized until the marrow appears, until it strengthens the bone within that the bone is softened, and this is the form of small alphbetization.</start_of_turn And it is estimated that from that area the vapors of the head expire.</start_of_turn>
And if the wound remains open for a long time, and it should be cured when it is consolidated.</start_of_turn
I do not see these two kinds of cautery in all my life, except in some men according to their fear; and leave it, for you, it is better to be healthy than to be burned, when it is possible; for the head is developed by the solution of continuity of its parts as we have testified in other members, and more when the head of the patient is of fiery nature.</start_of_turn
The first kind of cautery is better and more useful for you; and of that one and of this work we have health.
Chapter two.</start_of_turn>
Of the cautery of the head.</start_of_turn
When in all the head chronic pain and lasting pain occurs and it lasts in the disease for a long time, and when it is used of herbs and of poultices and of capsulars and of plasters and of butter and of vinegar and of broth and of eggs and of rosemary, and especially if it has already been cauterized with a cautery that they recount and that does not benefit it from any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the disease is of strong creation in its nature; and it is not fiery and does not find great heat, then that which cauterizes with another cautery leaves a little space.</start_of_turn And cauterize that on the nail of the heel up to the marrow is separated.</start_of_turn Incise the bone and uncover from the bone the quantity that we have recounted and cauterize that with a cautery in the posterior part of the head in the area where the wind is stopped. And withdraw your hand in help, and do not uncover the bone, for the disease for this finds great pain other than the pain of all the other cauteries of the head.</start_of_turn
I say this cautery in its place, for the cautery of which we cauterize the nails of the head and the occiput is more subtle than that which we cauterize the middle part of the head; and this is the way of it.</start_of_turn
Chapter three.</start_of_turn
Of the cautery of the ancient emigration.</start_of_turn

And care for that which is affected until it is healed
And if you wish, know that there are many medicines that combat these which I have written in the treatise of medicinal treatments

and it is called closed nails, because its head is like a nail with a curvature in which there is a small prominence in the middle of the area.</start_turn>

And if the quantity of the blood that is left behind by the specification of the wound is as great as most of it, elevate your hand so that the artery that is left behind does not suffer injury, so that there is no flow of blood.</start_turn

Chapter XXI
Of cautery for toothache
When toothache is caused by cold, or if it is too hot or does not yield to treatment with medicine, then do the following: either cauterize along the gum line or cauterize with fire.
Cauterizing along the gum line means that you take the edge of a piece of leather and put it into a pan of fire, and when it is red hot, you touch it to the edge of the tooth with your hand covered with cloth, and you keep it there until the tooth is numb.
And repeat that several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, immerse a sponge or cloth in the border of the diseased limb, and rest it on the painful tooth, and rest it on the ignited instrument until the instrument reaches the depth of the curvature of the tooth.
However, the use of the cautery with fire is that you must be attentive to the quantity of charcoal or instrument, and in the midst of them any roughness and the sharpness of the fire should not reach the mouth of the patient.
And if you have ignited the cautery, let it take the shape you wish, and rest it on the tooth and keep your hand there until the cautery is cooled; and do whatever you can so that the pain may subside or on this day or on the next day
And know that in order to prevent infection from that cautery that the patient should fill his mouth with good broth and keep it there for an hour, and then remove it; and this is the method of the cautery.
And cauterize as much as you can according to what is possible for you.<end_turn>

On cauterization for leprosy
Many books speak of cautery for great benefit, but it should not be used for the species of leprosy that causes putrefaction of fat and melancholy.
Therefore, when you wish to cauterize, consider whether the leprosy is acute or chronic and cured with what we have said in the division, neither too little nor too much; and fear lest the corruption should embrace the whole body and its completeness, for then cauterize on the head with three cauteries: one in the middle of the head, and two at the sides, and on the forehead above the eyebrows; and two at the back, over the nape of the neck or on the shoulder.
And finally, lay your hand over the cautery for a moment until a slight blistering appears on the bone, and from that the scales will be loosened; so that the expulsion of thick vapor is alleviated from them; and cauterize on the belly as required
If the leprosy has already spread over the body and is evident, it is necessary to cauterize in addition to the previous cauteries mentioned in the head; and on the tip of the nose, and two on the two cheekbones, and two on two vertebrae of the neck, and five on the vertebrae of the chest, and one on the chest near the shoulder, and two on the wrists, and two on the thumbs, and two on the knuckles, and two on the muscles, and two on the tendons of the thighs; and cauterize on all the joints of the fingers and toes, and on all the nails of the feet and on the teeth of the patient
And beware of the nerves that are above the ankle so that you do not burn them.
Many are cauterized with a cautery on the fifth toe bone and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the heel
Remember that the more cauteries you make, the greater the benefit and the greater the safety; and remember that the body is already stupefaied when there is no pain in the cautery, just as if they had never been applied
And know that the cauteries should be large or small according to the limb and the joints as it precedes the species of instruments
And take care that the cautery is well bound with a piece of cloth or bandage and with another care that it is not too tight

Capital ix.
The cold humors which infiltrate each part of the body cause great pain in the feet, which is usually called gout by physicians.
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery.

Therefore open the space between the patient's thighs, and gently push out that which is outside so that it escapes easily, and place your hand over that which remains to prevent it from escaping.
And if the swelling is great, then you must suture it; and care for that until it is healed.
And if it is slight, you need not fear that it will cause any harm because the swelling will restore itself and shrink.
If the swelling is diminishing on the side of the foot, you must draw out the surface of the foot, suspend the swelling with your hand, otherwise if you pull out from the incision, the patient will not notice anything.
And finally, close the incision, wash the area with salt-water; and care for the wound until it is healed.
Capital x.
The treatment of this great pain of the foot which comes from the outside of the foot.
The greatest of these is that which is engendered in the humors of the foot itself, and especially in children, for they suffer from this more and their bones are weakened thereby; and they cannot bear the heat of the sun because the fat in their limbs becomes soft and sticky at this time.

Every way of operating in such a case is to make the patient lie down on his side and gently push up the limb and put on a bandage; and circle it according to the quantity of humors which are contained throughout, and then press on that and pull down from the thumb of your hand so that the swelling is more concentrated in the middle of the circle, and finally open the space between the thighs to the extent that the incision does not exceed the breadth of the incision in phlegmatique swelling.

On the care of great importance of the navel.
The great importance of the navel is useful for many causes; or for cracks of the sac which is over the belly, and these are covered with the cloth or the gut according to what is necessary in other ruptures; or for healing which flows from veins or from intestines as it is said, or for wind that is restricted in it.

If it is for humidity, it is painful and is not hidden when you put your hand on it, nor is it constricted, nor is it swollen
And if it is for healing, the pus appears black and declining.
If it is for nothing, the pus is difficult, thick and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity
If it is for wind, the touch of it is painful
The operation is such that if the swelling of the navel threatens to burst from an artery, or a vein, or from wind, you must refrain from its cure, for in such a case fear and pain are imminent as you have been taught in the chapter where I spoke of the aftercare for an artery and a vein.
If the swelling of the navel threatens the intestines or the skin, then command the patient to sit upright; and place your hand around the navel circuit and command him to lie down between your thighs, and surround the area around the navel with a broad strip of linen; then extend the major part of the incision downwards to the groin; and join in the circuit with a strong suture or a needle and thread of good quality.

If you have found the skin, take hold of it with one hand; and cut away the excess of it.
May it be contrary to your artery or vein, then surround that part and return to your operation; take two needles and make two strong holes in those two fields and insert two needles into the circuit that you have made around the incision in the manner of a cross, which shall pierce; and strengthen the incision in four parts over the needles.

If the swelling of the navel is of fatty substance in it or for moisture, then command to uncover the incision as we have said and extract the fat or moisture which you find in it, and care for that which covers and consolidates the area.

Of castration
Wisdom has it that castration is forbidden in our laws, however I recall it in this book; and it is not necessary to recall it except for two cases. The one is when the physician is questioned about it, for he should know how to cure it. The other case is when we must castrate other animals for our food, such as pigs, horses, goats, and the like.
Therefore I say that castration is useful in two ways: by traction or by incision to the root
In that case where traction is useful, the way of performing the operation is to immerse the animal in cold water until the testicles are softened and limp and hanging down And then take hold of them with your hand until they are resolved and do not appear to be touching each other
And in castration that is useful by incision and cutting, grasp the animal and hold the knee of the testicles with your left hand
And then ligate the surgeon, and make an incision over every blood vessel with a section so that two veins protrude.
And then make the incisions more than enough that there may be no further tearing Do not worry about any bleeding from the wound, but rather the delicate skin over the veins
This method of castration is better than traction, for traction causes strong pain and often leaves any cause of the testicles because the animal desires to bite
And care for the wound until it is healed

De curacio de las fistulas que endeveno dejos.
The fistulas that arise in the lower parts of the legs are notable and numerous, and arise from the groin or in the space of the buttock.
And it is a fistula or swelling.
And when that swelling is old and corrupted by the white or putrid moisture, and some veins are seen to penetrate from these fistulas.
And those that penetrate are known because they are driven out by the evacuation and the wind; and some veins use the patient's evacuation, and it is very strong that it is driven out from them.
And from these fistulas some veins penetrate into the bladder, and into the marrow of the bone; and some penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the bone of the knee.
And it is known that a penetrating fistula that enters the groin is not penetrating, that you must tell the patient to lie down in the groin, and that you must attempt to remove the cause or the stone in the fistula when it is not crooked.
If it is crooked, then enter into that attempt with lead or horsehair until you sit on the vein or hold it in the groin.
And if you do not sit on that or if you do not succeed in any way in removing the cause of evacuation or stone or wind, as we have said, then it is known that it is not penetrating, and you must be content with the treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates the bladder or the marrow of the bone, it is known that it is of urine from that place and that it is forbidden to drink until the area is solidified by medical treatment.
And if it penetrates the thigh joint or the bone and causes pain in the limb, it is known that the vein has burst into the bone if it is not crooked, and causes pain in the limb of the part; and that from it urine is excreted; and that it is of no use in this treatment, nor is it solidified by this treatment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas, treatment is not enough, and the treatment of these is the work and uselessness of the doctors who have stopped it.
And in that one that is not penetrating and does not worsen, healing with iron is expected as I will tell you to recommend, and that which I have already tried and proved.
And it is that you must place the patient between your knees and elevate the legs above their level, the thighs are inclined towards the patient's belly, and then enter with a lead weight or stone if there is a fistula and it is crooked, until you see that the vein has returned to its place
And if the patient cries out in pain in the groin, then you must tell them to lie down in the groin.
And if you sit on the groin the vein has already burst through the skin without you having to uncover it, or that you sit between the groin and the hip or thigh, it is known that it is penetrating; and do not work on that, for it is not in this treatment.
I say, however, that this is healthy in some homes.
And as for the treatment by which it is hoped to succeed in this case, it is that you burn a cautery over the surface of the fistula according to the size of the fistula, as it has been said before, and you insert that burn into the fistula until it reaches the groin; and repeat that two or three times until you see that all the inflamed tissue surrounding the fistula has become soft like feathers from a sparrow.
And then care for those who are wrapped in gauze around the edges until all those tissues that have become soft have been removed, and care for that medicine that generates and consolidates the flesh, and if it is healed, it is good; but if not, it is known that it is not healed in any other treatment.
And if the vein enters but does not penetrate inside the groin, where it is in the groin, between that and the vein which is visibly red from flesh or fat, and sometimes the fistula breaks the surface of the skin, then dry the wound from the start of the fistula, and you will see it dry on the vein, and be free from the fistula from the root.
And finally soften those tissues that are joined together like needles of sparrow and do not remain from any cause
However, sometimes after surgery it happens that the wound comes out between you and your operation when you tighten those tissues, then it is better to burn with fire or acute medicine, because the burn on fire adjusts well many good things: it is the closing of those tissues that have been adjusted, and the excision of the excessive humidity.
And so treat those who are wrapped in cold clothes or are wrapped in thick clothes until the limb gets warm, and then treat the wound that is inflamed and hardened.
And so medicines that contain both styptic and excretory properties; when the limb is restored, it is already healed and does not fear recurrence.</end_of_turn>
However, if the fistula has already progressed into the belly of the buttocks and is prolonged on the surface of the body, then bring the intestine to the buttocks and inquire about that.</end_of_turn>
And therefore if you are certain and between you and her is wax of fat or flesh, and it is likely to penetrate, do not perform an operation on her, but rather by means of trust and hope.</end_of_turn
The cause is to administer in her one of three ways: either that you cauterize that which we have said; or that you drain that until you have restored the concavity of the limb so that you can easily remove the pieces and perform the cure; do not proceed without first draining lest you cause the wound to burst and contaminate the patient; and indeed take care of the patient immediately when she wishes it; or that you prolong that which we have said and order that pus which you drained from the buttocks be spread over the wound, as we have said, or use another sharp instrument, and mix the cauterized parts with the fistula, and strive to restore the limb to its normal state, and if the purulent discharge does not solidify, and the fistula remains open in the buttocks, and if there is still pus in the wound, you will be more curious about the patient.</end_of_turn> And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: when you insert the finger into the fistula, around the buttocks on the surface of the body and at the margin of the buttocks, the limb tries to perforate the extremity, that is to say as if with a needle to prepare the layers according to this method:
... and bring down in that flexible covering of flesh or around those; and put your finger into the fistula until you have restored the concavity of the limb.</end_of_turn
However, if it has penetrated the margin of the buttocks do not be afraid, for you will pull out the flesh from that wound as soon as you put your finger into the buttocks; withdraw the limb from the flesh and join the two ends together, and bind them; and leave them so for a day or two, and when the flesh has subsided from the bone, rejoin that which is between the two extremities of the flesh which were bound.</end_of_turn
And so treat the wound until it is consolidated and healed.</end_of_turn>
However, if the discharge from the fistula is not penetrating, do not attempt to make it penetrate in any way, but rather leave it where it is until it has healed naturally; and indeed do so for the wound to heal.</end_of_turn
The shape of the spatum spine concerning which the fistula is split: the curvature of which is not acute and the other part is obtuse, so that you do not cause any unnecessary bleeding, as sometimes happens.</end_of_turn
Suturing of wounds in which runs safety at the incision of those.</end_of_turn
Wounds are of two kinds, that is, either those that remain between the buttocks as if of cartilage, or those that are like pieces of grass.</end_of_turn And these are small and large, and they run from these to those and are one, and not many, and are outside the buttocks and in the extremities of the limb.</end_of_turn
However, those that are outside the buttocks should be sutured according to the months of little humidity, that is to say with citrine water or a little of salt dissolved in continuous water, and according to the color of the wound.</end_of_turn
And the cure of that which comes out of the bone is that you order the patient to move and expel until the bone has scabbed over and the wounds have disappeared.</end_of_turn Then you lie down and suspend your hand over his nails or that you hold them in your nail, and in this way you will prevent them from bleeding.</end_of_turn

From the wind and from the qualities of these things
The winds are of barley, or of wheat, or of ivy
And the wind is useful in two ways: one is by scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is by the wind itself
And this wind that is of scarification is done in two ways, that is by fire or by friction
And to the winds that are administered by scarification and extraction of blood there are fourteen parts of the body, of which one in which the winds are stopped is the ankle; and the fifth part from the knee downwards; and the winds from the chin downwards go beyond the mouth; and the winds from two spatulas; and the winds of alohost, which is at the end of the thigh; and the winds of two flames; and the winds of two braziers; and the winds of two cavities; and the winds of two cushions
The wind does not extract blood except from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and by this it does not take away the virtue of these things, just as in the case of phlebotomy; neither does it suffice that the wind should be done by fire or friction in any ailment that is useful for the evacuation of everything from the body
However, if necessary, we can cause a wound for an ailment or for a continuation, we will administer it at the beginning and at the end of the month, and in the middle of the month and at any other time as needed
And therefore, when in any case of these, and properly if it is in the third or half of the month, it is commanded that the wind should be done more than at any other time of the day or two or three hours
And the benefit of the wind from the neck is that when it confers gravity to the head and that which is effaced from the heels; however, it does not suffice that it should be a close evacuation of everything from the body
And this wind is in the place of the cephalic phlebotomy
It is not lawful to use it for those who are of complete madness, or in which there is congestion, because it gives great harm to that.

I command the attendant not to proceed too much with the knife, because the flesh is stripped of skin, and leaves the nerves and blood vessels exposed.

E las ventosas dels efantz e extenuatz so outras que las ventozas dels joves e de grosses corssas.
E la qualitat de pausar aquesta ventoza am foc sobre le membre es que extenda la meca am foc de lenha decentment denant una pauca candela de cera, e pausa aquella sobre le mieg de la vergua transversa en le mieg loc de la ventoza, per que le foc sia accendut enviro la partida dejos per que no sia comburit le cors del malaute.
E aprop sia pausada sobre le membre del malaute, e le dit sia sobre le trauc que havem dit, entro que quan tenem las ventozas e non indigem que osten le dit e que yesca la vapor sobre aquel trauc, lahoras la ventoza sira tantost dissolvuda
E prop igneys la meca segon la sua manieyra, e itera aquela si indigeyssas de aquela.

E aquesta es la forma de lu: E aquesta ventoza quant plus es gran, tant es milhor, per que puya recebre gran quantitat de aygua.

Chapter First.</end_of_turn>
Summary and collection from this fracture of bones, from which the previous preface is necessary, before we begin the recollection of fractured limbs and various parts of each.</end_of_turn Therefore, let us speak in the prologue of this chapter about the summaries of the discourse; and the chapters that follow are intended to bring to light the artifices and to settle the truth of those things; so that you and those who wish to learn this noble art may know or learn it from you.</end_of_turn
Therefore, I say that when an accident of fracture or dislocation or twist or any similar thing happens, the hour immediately covers that you should begin with cold compresses or apply an aleatory, or whatever helps, if it does not impede any cause, as befits prudence, or if it is the heat that has caused the accident, or if the person is young and robust, or if it is cold weather.
And let food be moderate in salads of fresh herbs and boiled meats of calves and crabs; and forbid fatty meats and feed that is full of fat, and all food that fills the veins of the stomach, except that you follow the rule of caut dressing, and do not fear the effusion of matter from the limb.</end_of_turn
Then return the patient to their first position as soon as possible.</end_of_turn>
And when the broken bone begins to be restored, the hour covers that the patient should not be given nourishing foods of great viscosity, such as porridge made with flour and water, broth, eggs, cheese, fish, beef, fat, and barley, and in this regimen there is a coagulation of the fracture that is more useful and more gentle.</end_of_turn
Therefore, you know that bones that are fractured in the first degree and in decrepitude cannot be continued to be fractured and consolidated according to their nature because of the drying up of the limbs.</end_of_turn
However, nature must adjust and remember that the fractured bone of any part whatever, is of such great size that it adheres and strengthens itself as soon as it is bound together, until it comes to the end of movement and rest, just as with fire at the beginning, except that no cause hinders that.</end_of_turn
Therefore, in this case it is necessary to stop the patient's food, food in which there is gravity and viscosity and greatness, as we have said.</end_of_turn
Therefore, you know that the species of fracture are diverse according to the diversity of the limb, for the fracture of the thigh bone is different from the fracture of the head bone; and the fracture of the foot bone is different from the fracture of the forearm; and so on with all the other limbs.</end_of_turn
And I remember all kinds of fracture, explained in a distinct chapter from the others.</end_of_turn
There are many different fractures within each category.</end_of_turn And the species of fracture within each category are diverse; for example, a fractured bone in its star may be fractured in a different way from one that occurs in its marrow; some fractures are simple, while others are compound, proceeding from the break of the bone itself and not from the surrounding tissue, just as it is in writing when prepared to write, and it is a fractured bone with a wound and disruption in the head, and a fractured fissure of the bone.</end_of_turn
And in every case it is an evil or torment proper in restoring them according as will be remembered from their distinctness in the various places.
Sign of fracture of the bone. And for this is known as fracture of the bone: it is twisting of the limb, and from that protrusion and appearance of the limb to the sensation, and so from that when it is compressed with your hand
And therefore when there is no apparent twisting of the limb or even if it is not suspected, you must touch the bone gently when you touch it so that the patient does not feel great pain, for here there is no fracture
There is also the possibility of slight twisting or small fracture, whereupon you must not press on it with your hand and compress it; there must be a pause in relation to the medicines of which you remember at that moment; and immediately for stricture of the marrow
And you must know that when the limb is bent and is not fractured into two or other parts that do not affect it in its stability, as for example the whole part of its substance, the hour is that you begin to rectify it immediately after the cause has ceased.
And if it recurs after the cause has ceased, leave it for a few days until the swelling subsides; and then support it in any way that you can, as by raising and binding.
And you must know that the restoration of the limb and its convalescence is easier than that of the bone in which the fracture has occurred
And so do all things according as will be remembered in each case.
May be if there are fractures in the bone, it is necessary to extend this limb fractured in two parts, whether it is the hand or the foot; or with your hand if the limb is small; or with two cords or with one cord and the hand.
And let your position be such that you can support the limb relaxed according to its natural figure, while the fractured parts are extended from the limb, so that you can restore those adhesions with engineering and in any way that you can in their places.
And take care that you do not cause further pain or injury to the patient by your operation of healing; and follow the treatment that you apply to a bone with another companion in many other forms
And you must take advantage at that moment of your touch with your hand in order to rectify any other cause, and if there is sometimes any other cause, rectify that and support that for the amount of your skill
And avoid violent extension and compression, just as wise doctors do who make use of cautery after their operation, or who make use of constriction in the limb in the way that we have seen in the operation of their veins.
And the quality of the stricture of the limb is that which I recommend; for you must know that fractured limbs are diverse in their size and greatness and in their form
And as for those that are small such as the arm and the finger and the toe and the like, the hour is that the covering should be of soft material.
And as for those that are large such as the thigh or the chest, cover that with firm and hard covering, which connects the great limb firmly and strengthens that throughout its extent without causing any bruising
And so do all things, pause the ligament conveniently at the place of that fracture with three covers or four as the limb deserves; and strengthen your hand a little on the ligament.
And so look at the most prominent part of the place of the fracture, and strengthen less than that where you have strengthened the place of the fracture And so lengthen the covering of the place of the fracture a little, and soften the stricture little by little, until you have taken away a great part of the limb
And thus take another instrument and wrap that other bandage around the limb to be bound firmly; and when the bandage has been placed in its place, proceed with the operation in the manner described previously concerning the first bandage.
And if there is a swelling in the area of the fracture, or if the limb is twisted, leave it as it is in such cases; otherwise do not touch it for any reason.
And place another instrument over it, and tightly bind over these bandages as much as necessary; if there is no swelling or oozing from the wound, and when the oozing has ceased and the swelling has subsided; leave that for a few days; and then remove the supports gradually as necessary
The supports of the major limb are of various kinds, and should be formed skillfully; or of wood; or of palm leaves; and the width of each support should be as follows: ...
However, the support which is placed over the fracture should be larger and wider than the others, and its length should be according to the size of the limb; and grasp the supports with another instrument according to your previous instructions; and tie them securely as we have said previously, so that the support is the most stable in the area of the fracture and the more the limb is elongated, the weaker the support should be
And it must be ensured that the threads are of moderate thickness and flexibility, and are of silk; and if the threads are thick, like those used for surgery in other places, it is a great error when the support is removed and equality is not restored
Subtle threads are not suitable for this purpose, for you will not achieve sufficient support in this way, and it must not be the case that there is less than a finger's breadth between the supports
And if the patient is suffering from excessive stiffness of the limbs at the extremities, support the limb in the places mentioned until the stiffness has disappeared without causing further injury
Some bandages for fractures are like ointments, and others are like disruptions of the cord, and I remind you of this in the chapter concerning singularity
Remember that every fractured limb is not straight at first; the reason for this is that when the limb is large, it is not appropriate to support it on the bandages immediately; rather wait a few days or even more, according to your estimate of the risk of oozing
This is the method of dressing which the Ancients used to restore fractures, dislocations and twists.
Method of dressing similar to that of the ancients, suitable for multiple complex fractures, especially for women and men, because of which it is not heated or cooled by the air: and take powdered charcoal, which is the middle of wheat that remains after the wheat has been ground.
And keep it moist like this, but do not make it wet; and cover it with a cloth that is not too thick or too thin; and use this as a dressing
Another method for plastering is for fracture, dislocation and sprain: recipe of asafoetida, of lapdanum, of acacia, of enula, and marigold, which is ground from a thousand grains of Salvago, by weight of two drams. Five of mirra and aloen by weight of one dram. Twenty of alochil by weight of two drams. All of these are triturated and sieved and mixed with water, with oil or with egg white if the patient's wound is raw; and use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores the broken bones pleasantly, and gives comfort to many people.
Another method for plastering which gives comfort for fracture and sprain: recipe of marigold and white alum at the rate of two drams. Five of mirra and aloen by weight of one dram. Six of acacia by weight of one dram. Two hundred of beeswax by weight of two hundred.
All of them are powdered in a mortar with a rough stone, are mixed, and are moistened with water or liquid and administered

Another method of dressing that restores broken bones: take figs and poppy seeds; mix them up and make a dressing of them
A short method of dressing that promotes the restoration of bone fractures and when you desire resolution of the remaining swelling: mix powdered elderberry, chamomile and violet flowers, barley flour, all in equal parts Put everything in a decoction and keep it warm, if the limb is not scorched
If it is scorched, however, keep it comfortable with lukewarm water or with vinegar and use it
Another method of dressing that is more powerful in resolving this is when the swelling is severe: mix elderberry and linseed seeds, barley, meadowsweet, marjoram, violets, chamomile, all in equal parts and fennel; put everything in a decoction and keep it warm with vinegar or water, or with wine, according to the quality of the limb and the degree of swelling
Hippocrates does not say that in the free air it should be placed over the fractured limb in order to promote its restoration, but rather that it should be covered with wax and oil and not otherwise; and I recommend that you rather use an intermediate degree between thickness and thinness
Indeed in Gaul they put it over the fractured limb in order to promote its restoration and the causes of its pain, such as small inflammation or cold, as well as its causes that we have recommended.
Method of dressing that relieves the lesion and pain: mix millet, chickpea flour, ground fennel seeds or pennyroyal seeds, elderberry, salt, all in equal parts; grind them together and sift them, and make a dressing of them
The quantity should be according to the degree of swelling that must be left on the limb, and if there is no pain or swelling or the bone is not fractured, it is not appropriate to remove it for a long time. And if there is acute pain or swelling or inflammation in the area, then in that hour you must cover it or remove it immediately, and keep the dressing on it
Take linen cloth and marine sponge soaked in warm water, and immerse that in lukewarm water; with that wash the area until the swelling and pain disappear; then put on a bandage with a soft bandage soaked in strong vinegar and olive oil or olive oil alone, and keep it on for a night until you are sure that the cautery has healed, and that the swelling of the limb has subsided, and that the pain has gone away.
And do the same with the stricture and put on a small dressing and do not bind it tightly for your initial constriction, but rather do it gradually as it improves.</start_of_turn>
And if sometimes the swelling and the redness and the pain and the inflammation and all these things have already subsided, and digestion of the dressing and the stricture has begun, then in that case you must repeat it as before, just as you did at the beginning when you put on the dressing.</start_of_turn>
And if no other cause appears in the limb of those that we have mentioned, then do not remove it for three or four days or five or seven days.</start_of_turn And some people keep it like this for xx days according to the appearance of the limb, as we have said, until the fracture adheres, and when the coagulacion of the marrow over that has taken place.</start_of_turn
And when you adjust in the stricture more than in your initial stricture, and when you adjust in the nourishment of the patient's diet, according to the memory of that.</start_of_turn
Indeed if sometimes the limb of the fracture has dried out and become flexible again more than when you first covered it, know that nutrition is prohibited in that case; and therefore take away from that lukewarm water for three days; and loosen the stricture a little, and by this operation restore nutrition to the limb, and it will recover quickly.</start_of_turn
Indeed those who restore the fracture of the limb do not do as others when they do not restore it at the beginning, according to the custom; and they restore it according to their whim, which is an error in the operation of them, and is dangerous, and if they do that which increases the pain in the limb when it is free, they will aggravate it with that which they do.</start_of_turn
And I have never seen anyone do that, for it is more reasonable that it does not happen.
Chapter two: Of fractures when they happen in the head.</end_of_turn>
There are various kinds of fractures, and their figures are diverse, and their causes are different, for some fractures are caused by impact to the space, and the impact hinders all the bone within the cavity, which remains fractured, just as when it happens in the wrist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called fracture of the bone; or the space impacts some part of the bone, and impacts the marrow without passing the incision through the back of the bone; and this kind of fracture is called absolute elevation.</end_of_turn>
And the swelling of these two fractures is great or little, and of a fracture that is contracted or contained; and the cause of these is impact with the palm of the hand or with the edge of the foot, and the like.</end_of_turn
And this fracture is penetrating that has already approached the bone which is left fractured; or it is on the face of the bone, and the swelling of these two fractures is great or little.</end_of_turn
Or the fracture is that which is hidden in the bone, in the substance of the small vessel, and for this reason it is called capillary fracture.</end_of_turn
And the fracture is caused by impact or by chance or by impact of the foot and it leaves an indentation in any lamina of the bone to the parts adjacent, and it is fractured in the hollow part just as when it happens to the nails when they are impacted and broken through.</end_of_turn
Mostly it is caused in bones of soft texture, as for example their heads.</end_of_turn
And thus all these stationary fractures are like separated stars.</end_of_turn And I find it necessary to remind you of everything in this place.</end_of_turn
And I know all these kinds of fractures by detection on them and by questioning them in order to detect any underlying corruption of the bone that is over them.</end_of_turn
The capillary fracture is known by this that it is discovered on the bone, and it is excised, and it is limited over it with a tent, so that the fracture appears black.</end_of_turn
In the treatment of fracture attention should be paid at the beginning to the signs of the illness, and when sometimes for the signs that may signify for significance appears with vomiting of bile, extension, loss of consciousness, loss of voice, syncope, fever, and acute pain in the joints and stiffness of those.</end_of_turn
And if sometimes non-violent accidents occur you expect health, the hour you begin the treatment of them.</end_of_turn
Which cause is that if it is verified in the beginning like that which is verified in the days of spring, the hour you must study in the marrow of the bone thirteen days according to all custom.</end_of_turn
And if it is in the summer days, the hour you must cover the bone thirteen days starting from the seventh day, having to keep that which is left of the bone corrupt from the marrow, and to take care of the accidents which we have recommended.</end_of_turn
And if the fracture has already reached the marrow covering the brain, and it is contracted and contained, the hour you must insert the fractured parts and bind them, as I recommend to you.</end_of_turn
And that you take the head of the illness that is inflamed, and you uncover the bone according to custom and manage as you are able according to the figure of the inflammation, and that you are curious about the illness.</end_of_turn
And if it happens to you that you detect the bone, flux of blood or caut abscess, the hour you oppose it with what covers it, and that you cover the area with clean cloth soaked in vinegar and oil, and make the swelling subside until the abscess is sedated; and be sure to drain the blood; and start the treatment by applying the bandage to the bone and opening the wound.</end_of_turn
And this is according to two methods of operation.</end_of_turn
And the first method is that you insert the bone with a straight incision, and this is how you do it: And you give another incision a little wider than the first; and this is how you do it.</end_of_turn
And you give more of the latter incision.</end_of_turn
And know that you must give your name as an inscription, for some of them are more lazy than others; and some of them are shorter than others and are at the back of the order of their extremities, and they are made of iron or venomous material.
And use of them [instruments] makes it easier to perform the incision on the inscription so that you do not break the head and leave it behind.
And if the bone is strong, hard, then cover that you pierce in the circumference of it before you administer the inscription, which are called superficial not deep
They are not called thus except that those who do not stop the term of the bone until they are close to it, because the superficial part of the limb or margin over that which the head of the limb is left behind appears like a margin or small circle, which prohibits it from being submerged and passing through the substance of the bone
And it is convenient that you take a large number of these superficial incisions, of which each one agrees with the substance of each bone, except in those cases where in all tests of the limb the extremity that is acute in length and breadth is such that the quantity in length and breadth is according to the quantity of substance of that limb.
And this is the form of three species of incisions: The quality of piercing in the circumference of the broken bone is that you stop the incision on the bone and rotate that around which you have tied it until you know that the bone has already been penetrated; and then change the incision to another place, and stop when there is between all the distance the quantity of the thickness of the ray or around that
And indeed incisions are made with the inscription when there is between each break of the bone, and make that one more subtle than you can over that in order to finish levitating, as we have said, until you have eradicated the bone, or with your hand, or by any other cause for some tremor that has appeared in it, such as nails and fine forceps
And know that you must take great care that the inscription does not touch any cause of infection.
And therefore when you have pierced the circumference of the bone, and if it is continuous with the infection if it is continued with it, then extract that, know that you should burn and cauterize that with the substance of the infection that is in the bone or another cause similar to an incision, but indeed that you must make it more tense and subtle than the others
And if there remains any small parts of bones and fragments, then take that which is convenient for you from the causes of the ailments; and indeed take care of the wound with lint and dressings as we have said.
And another way of operating is light, long, which says dissection Gaul and the lauzing for great profit; and this is the saying of it: it is necessary for you at the beginning to begin to discover the part of the bone of the limb in which the fracture is the most vehement and most manifest, until when you have discovered that part and you have stopped leaving that limb that the incision is slow and peaceful of which this is the form:
And that the blunt part is round and does not touch any cause, and the acute part is of it in two directions before and after in length, as sometimes; that the blunt part is adjusted to the infection with the face of the acute incision on the bone.
And indeed pierce about the inscription with a little mallet so that you can insert all the bone easily as if it were rotated, and you will be sure of the safety that it will not happen by chance that you fear in any way, and if the physician was the most foolish of all men and the most ignorant of them; certainly, and if he was asleep.
And if there remains any adjacent cause to the bone of the cavity in several places, pierce that one with the extremity of the incision that is blunt, and deliver that one with ease, which is delivered from it without document and without fear.
And if the bone is not pierced into the cavity, and what is broken or remains of the bone is the face of it, and remains in it in asperities and subtle fragments, then know that you must burn that asperitat and extirpate those fragments with subtle reasons for those for which you have prepared the number, of various quantities so that you can easily manage them in all places and make the most of them according to what you lose in your operation that broken bone and its figure.
And know that you must administer in your reason the greatest part of those reasons at the beginning of the reasons, and indeed use the greatest part of the subtle of them, and do not stop until you have completed the greatest part and the most subtle of all those.
Indeed in any other small fractures capillary and subtle fracture, know that you must take care according to what you have lost for the rectification of it.
It is because of this that no learned person has been able to explain it in its entirety. Therefore, as we have said before in great fractures...
If the swelling is rectangular when you radiate it out, then take as much of the plaster as the amount of the wound and immerse it in scented oil, and place it over the orifice of the wound; and take another bandage doubled or tripled and immerse it in wine and scented oil and place it over the first bandage, and do so until the pus comes out willingly from that place, without causing damage; and then give him some lard around that area, and do not tighten it until the wound is whole only as much as the wound itself
And leave it like this for a day or two until you are certain that the burn has subsided; and then remove the bandage and administer medicines which are useful for drying, such as linseed and barley flour, henbane and marjoram, and similar things to these
And it is necessary that you grind these medicines into powder and sprinkle them over the wound; and in general, give any medicine that has the property of drying, such as alum or mercury.
And take heed of your art that the wound in your care should be dry; do not put anything greasy on it or anything else; and do not let it become infected; for when it is applied to the swelling of the head, it corrupts that and impoverishes that, and brings about illness in the patient
And take care in the head, as when it is solidified it breaks the bones more and especially when the care is negligent; and it is black on its surface; and therefore consider that if an accident happens to the patient, the things that we have said are dangerous for him, because it is perilous in every way.
And if there is no blackness except for the medicine that has been stopped, and it is in virtue of that medicine that causes that blackness, then take three parts of vinegar and two parts of scented oil, in the proportion of three to two.</start_of_turn> And mix it with these ingredients a bandage, and place it on the swelling; and care for that with the spices of care which you consider to be useful until it is healed.</start_of_turn>

Of the restoration of the nose when it is fractured.</start_of_turn
Know that the nose is not fractured but simply bowed down somewhat, or one of these has been softened, so that in it there are two bones, for the part that is left is cartilaginous and is not fractured, and does not cause it any damage but swelling and pain and numbness.</start_of_turn
Moreover, if one of the two parts is fractured, then you must insert a little support in the nose, and stabilize that fracture with the index finger and the thumb, until the nose returns to its natural shape.</start_of_turn And do this with ease, and take care that you do not cause any pain to the patient during this operation.</start_of_turn
And if the fracture is in the lower part of the nose, and you say that it does not matter, then you must make it equal with the extremity of the ray where the thickness is small.</start_of_turn
And if the fracture is in two parts, you must make it look like that.</start_of_turn
And cover its restoration on the first day of the fracture if possible; and if not, then leave it for a while or two until the burn subsides.</start_of_turn
And put in the extremity of the nose a wad of linen, if the fracture is in one part, or two cushions, if the fracture is in two parts, and make them of such thickness that they fill the cavity of the nose.</start_of_turn
And tell the old restorers that the cushions should be bound at the edges, and should be changed throughout the day, even though I do not see it; for you must know that the wad should be bound with almond paste with powdered charcoal; and do so until the bone is firm and the cartilage is solidified.</start_of_turn
And in some cases put sponges inside the nose instead of a cushion, because it is better for swelling; and that the patient should not be prohibited from inspiration even if the fracture of the nose is violent, for the patient will recover more quickly.</start_of_turn
This matter is not necessary for you; and if you wish, do this, and if you wish, do that.</start_of_turn
And if another bruise appears after the burn subsides, plaster the nose with wax or with soot moistened in wine and scented oil, or with vinegar.</start_of_turn
May it be that if the cautery does not happen to slip, then cover that part with meal of size and with a powder of burnt chaff with an album of honey; and immediately stop over it with a sponge, and do not leave it exposed for any reason.
If the bones of the nose are fractured in a slight or great degree, then split them open, and extract those with instruments that are suitable for them; and immediately close the wound, and care for that which encloses and consolidates, and apply plasters as necessary
And if there is a wound in the nose, then care for that which is causing the bleeding and administer lead tubes until it is completely healed.

Restoration of the mandible when it is fractured
When the mandible is fractured and the fracture is not accompanied by bleeding, keep the fracture from displacement only if it is clearly displaced, and not fractured into two parts and bent outwards. In such a case, its sensation is light
Therefore, if the fracture is on the right side, insert the left index finger into the patient's mouth; and in the same way, if the fracture is on the left mandible, insert the index finger of the right hand; and grasp with that the swelling of the fracture outwards, with your other hand at the opposite side of the bone; thus you will easily equal the amount.
If the fracture of the mandible has already been separated into two, then administer extension of two parts according to rectitude until it is possible to equal them
If there is displacement of teeth with disruption, then strengthen those that you expect to remain in place with gold or silver or gutta percha; and immediately stop over the fractured mandible, and immediately stop over the duplicate tissue, and stop over the large pulp in place appropriately, or one piece of gutta percha equal to the length of the mandible; and tie that down according to what is appropriate for the libandage of the tooth and that which is convenient for the application, until it is not destroyed
Command the patient to rest and tranquility, and abstain from eating spicy foods for him
And if you see that the figure has already been altered in some way, then you will cover it up and take it off on the third day; and immediately correct what has already been altered of it and plaster that with powder of mill, with an album of honey, or with meal of size, because you must not leave it uncovered, and stop over the plaster sponge
And thus when it is fixed and adjusted that plaster over it, and the arrangement of the bone is not altered, leave it in place, do not take it out until it is healed and strengthen the fracture; for if the swelling of this fracture is not dispelled in three periods, it will not be healed
And if another wound occurs after the cautery, then administer what has been said above in the case of bleeding until it is healed, and remove that wound
And if the fracture is accompanied by bleeding, consider whether it is a fracture of the bone separated or sutures; in this case you are ordered to remove those sutures with what is convenient for the removal of those of the torment
And if the wound is wide, then you will enlarge it with the flebotome according to the quantity of your need
And when you have finally removed those sutures, and those that you will not remove, then you will close the wound if it is wide; otherwise, stop over that one of the plasters which you consider convenient and care for that, until it is healed

Restoration of the jaw when it is fractured
When the jaw is fractured from the front towards the back of the teeth, and that fracture is caused by one of three things.
Or it is fractured, or separated, or is separated into two parts without causing sutures; and it is desirable for the restoration of it; or it is just that it has occurred in the sutures, and it is difficult to restore it; or it is just that the fracture is accompanied by bleeding
And the operation in that case, when the fracture is accompanied by bleeding, is that two assistants be present, so that one may hold the fractured jaw and the other extend the cheek towards that part
And immediately bind the fracture with the said strings until the shape of it is restored according to what you cover, and not in too little or too much prominence
If the pain persists despite the extension, then let him rest his hand from the patient, hoping that some degree of the swelling will subside; and let the size of the elevation depend on the quantity of the need; extend and elevate the foot and cover the swelling with your hand until the fracture is reduced.
If it is not possible to retract the limb from the socket, in order that it does not slip further, then let the patient rest his face on his chest, and place a cushion under his arm, supporting it with a smaller cushion of equal size.
And the attendants must support the limb under the socket until the bone of the foot is elevated above the level of the socket, and when the fracture is reduced, grasp those parts which are above with your thumb and index finger
Even if the fracture is displaced and the limb is hanging down, let him rest on that and extract those satagias with ease
If it is retained in the bone, let you make an incision of the limb with one of the instruments which you have prepared beforehand, since you have already rested the foot from the discomfort which it caused; and the discomfort is of the kind of fist or nail of which this is the shape
It is similar to a wound of which this is the cavity; and let its width be according to what you need of it, according to the greatness of the bone or the thinness of it.
Let its length be as it is possible for the operation; that there be two limbs always, sometimes one limb is broad and the other narrow.</start_turn>
And if the disruption of the membrane which you have incised when you have extracted the foreign body from the bone is wide, and you are sure of its stability, then you adjust the two lips of the membrane together with sutures.</start_turn
And if the disruption is slight, or if you fear excessive bleeding, then you must cover the membrane with gauze and powder according to the quantity of the wound.</start_turn
And if bleeding should occur, let you apply pressure to the wound with wine vinegar and oil of rosemary and wine, and rest upon it.</start_turn
And finally, that the splint should not rest on the broken bone; and so that you see the patient every day, since when the ligament is softened or the splint is already softened, then you must rectify that and strengthen the bandage.</start_turn><end_turn>
And place the patient’s hand over the limb’s collar, and leave the hand resting from the limb for him to sleep with a small cushion; so that in this way the limb’s attendants are elevated from the side of this, and therefore the fracture of the foot is elevated with the elevation of the muscle; or that the arm is bound to the limb’s collar.</start_turn><end_turn
Do not remove the bandage if no bleeding occurs at the site or excessive bleeding, within twelve days.</start_turn><end_turn>
And renew the plaster if you have seen the face of the limb to it, and adjust in the stiffness and restore that and leave it until the fracture of the foot is restored and is coagulated.</start_turn><end_turn
And is strengthened and comforted according to the month in eighty days, and several visits in various homes are sufficient in a month of time of that.</start_turn><end_turn

And therefore when it is fractured in the limb – and it is fractured in the middle of the limb – and is not known except by touch, then according as the figure of the fracture forces you to prepare the limb and reduce that according to the natural figure in every way that is possible for you.</start_turn><end_turn

Chapter VII.</end_of_turn>
Of the restoration of the fracture of the foot.</end_of_turn>
The foot has several veins that are fractured in the middle of the bone and there; more the extremities of the limb move backwards that so cicatrize and diminish.</end_of_turn
And concerning the accidents of the limb when the middle of the bone is fractured, it is that it inclines to the inner parts and causes great pain, and difficulty in walking, and coughing, and vomiting of blood; and it is declared in the cavity of the fractured bone and is not hidden from feeling.</end_of_turn
And the restoration of the limb is that you rest the patient on the two sides, and suspend between the buttocks of the limb a cushion; and then press the muscles of the limb, and adjust the flanks of the limb to the greatest of two sides, and stretch your hand over the area and execute the operation of the limb and in the equalization as much as is possible and as it is convenient, until you restore the shape of the bone as it was before.</end_of_turn
And thus pause over the plaster and stop and pause over the staple of a spatula of obsidian or of ivory and of its like in suspension, because you wrap that around it; and gently encircle that over the fractured bone that it is not crushed; and keep stretching that which is strict downward; and consider the ligament at all times, and when it is softened stretch that also.</end_of_turn

Chapter VIII.</end_of_turn
Of the restoration of the back when it is fractured.</end_of_turn
Know that the fracture of the back does not crack completely but in places that follow the two; and from the extremities of the limb from the front part does not happen except for what is cartilaginous.</end_of_turn And you must know that it is not hidden from feeling, you must inquire about it from those who know it.</end_of_turn
And the restoration is thus that you embrace the fracture as it is said according to the possible manner, except that you embrace as much as covers, and then plaster and strengthen the fractured bone with a staple, if you deem it necessary of that.</end_of_turn
And if the fracture of the back is declining to the inner parts, then it happens to the patient severe pain and puncture, just as if it were a puncture that happened to him who has pleuracy; and for that the bone puts on the membrane; and it happens to the difficulty of handling, and coughing, and vomiting of blood; and this is of great difficulty of treatment.</end_of_turn
And indeed the Ancients have invented in that way that they can move without bending.</end_of_turn
And from them it is said: cover that you stop feeding the patient who caused inflammation and swelling, so that the belly is uninflated and is extended, and the fracture is fixed to the parts outside.</end_of_turn
May we avoid this, lest it should cause unnecessary bleeding, if not otherwise; and if it has already happened, then it will help to prevent further bleeding.
I say to you that it is necessary to suspend it from the wind and that it should suffice for a while; for in this way it is like reasoning, but I fear that the wind will drive the moisture to the wound for its weakness.
I say to you: cover the wound with a bandage that is already immersed in cautery oil, and leave fine powder between the ribs until it is full; let the ligature be gentle when you wrap it around the circumference; and do the same with healing the disease with feeding and medicine
And if it causes violent constriction of the disease that does not suffer from this, and if you put the instrument through the wound, remember over the disease, for when you cover the wound, uncover the broken rib, and do the same with the instrument that preserves the belly, as is usually done, and that they come out easily, and take away that one.
And do the same with the two lips of the wound, if it is large, by stitching, and care for that which is under plaster until it is healed.</start_turn>
And if there is bleeding from the wound, immediately cover it with powdered charcoal in scented oil and hold it over the wound, and let the disease be cured with what covers the bleeding.</start_turn>
And rest on the side on which you are lying, until it is healed.</start_turn
