Restoration of fracture of the vertebra of the thigh and of the heel.
Some veins sometimes fracture the bones of the heel, and sometimes to them it is necessary to apply an at traction, just as it is with the vertebrae of the thigh. And when this happens to someone and you want to know if he is well or not, consider that sometimes the veins are already softened and relaxed and sometimes they are soft and limp and dead and you cannot move them neither extend them nor flex them without causing them pain, if you tighten them they say that it is not well, and in such cases of adversity it is fatal.</start_turn
And if you touch them and find them constricted with the teeth and pierced, then you know that the bone of the limb is saved and the disease will heal with care.</start_turn
And if you see the vertebrae of the thigh like this and you want to know if it is well or not, consider the weight of the limb.</start_turn
Sometimes when it is softened, it is necessary to do what is necessary in the greatest number of cases, and when you lie over the two thighs, you feel the breeze and the evacuation of urine is forced from you, knowing that this is fatal, and you should not work on their care.</start_turn
May there be no other cause of this, for the cause is better and lighter.</start_turn
And the care of them is that you perforate with a cautery needle at the sensation of the bleeding that stops over the fractured vertebra, covered with scented oil alone, or with pieces of ground glass; and hold over that any vein that gives blood until the bleeding stops.</start_turn
And hold one of the existing and comfortable plasters, and strengthen over that which is ligament; and command the patient to rest and be calm and not to sleep on the side where he feels pain until he is healed.</start_turn

And if the femur is fractured at the thigh end, and it is the end of the limb, then cover that part with the left hand on the buttocks and hold the fractured bone with the right hand as much as possible; and hold over it the plaster and bandage, if you do not mind, and strengthen that.</start_turn
And if you feel the heel fractured in it, then rest over that, and keep that, and care for the wound with the care that is usually done until it is healed.</start_turn

Restoration of the limb.</start_turn
The bones of the limb often break, and when they break, the fracture of them is nothing but a communication in the extremities of these and they are inscribed in the length and decline towards the inward parts; and it happens to the patient pain in the area and puncture, and the limb is stiff when fractured.</start_turn
The restoration of the limb is that you extend your hand over that which is over the fracture which is the shape of the limb.
If the fracture is at the extremity of the limb alone, then you embrace that part which is askew according to the proportion that it is displaced until it is restored to its natural position.</end_of_turn>
More so if the fracture is in the long bones or that already declines to the lower parts, then you make the patient lie on his belly until he is prepared for the restoration of that fracture.</end_of_turn And therefore when you have restored that, suspend your hand over the bandage, and then pause over the splinter of bone or cartilage, and hold tightly over the place where you do not fear puncture of the fracture or removal of the splinter.</end_of_turn
And embrace the concave part with that which lies over that which prevents the stricture according to equality, and command the patient to lie on his side or across his chest.</end_of_turn
More so if the accidental burn occurs, then you cease the extension of the limb and the restoration until the accidental burn has subsided, and pause over it until that which is before has departed; and then return to the restoration of the limb, and hold tight as before.</end_of_turn
And if it happens in the heel bones or they are fractured, then you must treat them.</end_of_turn>

Treatment for the fracture of the adjutorium.</end_of_turn>
The adjutorium is that which is between the hip bone and the head of the femur.</end_of_turn>

And the other way is that the patient should be placed lying down on his shoulder and suspend the hand of the hip over the ligament; and command two assistants that one of them hold what is above the fracture with his hands; and the other hold his legs; and whichever of them extends to his part.</end_of_turn
And if you want the extension to be stronger, then you must tighten over the fracture with the ligament and over that with the other ligament, and whichever of the two assistants extends both of his parts.</end_of_turn
Therefore if the fracture is close to the extremity of the muscle, then you must cover that half of the ligament over the trochanter and the other half the fracture must be over the hip bone.</end_of_turn
Similarly if the fracture is near the hip bone, then you must cover that ligament over that place and that hip bone.</end_of_turn

Chapter XXIII.</end_of_turn
About dislocation.</end_of_turn>
Dislocation is the sudden displacement of any joint of the limb, because it is prohibited from movement, and it is accompanied by the deformation of the limb, and causes great pain and damage to the patient.</end_of_turn
Therefore when an injury occurs in some dislocation, it is necessary to perforate immediately so that it can be reduced, and do not delay in reducing it, for if it is delayed, the limb is swollen and strong, and it is difficult to reduce the dislocation.</end_of_turn
And so, do not move or stretch during the time of the apostemacy, because vomiting brings spasms and pain to the bowels.
When this happens, cover the patient's face with a towel, and immediately stop vomiting; then bring cold water and oil to the member, and gently reduce it.</end_of_turn>
And all parts should be treated with the water from which the memory will remain in their place.</end_of_turn>
And thus I have ordered the heads of dislocation according to what precedes fracture; from the upper part of the body inwards to the lower part outwards.</end_of_turn

On the reduction of the dislocation of the muscle
Be aware that the muscle is not dislocated in three ways, of which one is that it is dislocated from the part of the tibia to the part below
And the second is that it is dislocated from the part under the muscle, and this is usual; and it is not dislocated from the back for the shoulder; and it is not dislocated from the front for the nerves
And mostly it is dislocated outwards beyond the tibia, and more so in those in which the flesh is little, willingly it is dislocated; more in those in which there are many bones, it is forced out with difficulty
And often this happens to the bones by percussion or by chance, and the muscle of it is loosened from the tendon, and is cured as it has already been dislocated
Therefore, when you are aware of this, proceed in the treatment of it
And it is known that the dislocation is at the lower part of the tibia; therefore you must distinguish between the dislocated muscle and the normal muscle, because you find among these different appearances; and you find at the head of the muscle a concavity facing towards the tibia as much as a drop of oil; and to the patient it is not possible to reduce the hand to the ankle, nor to move it in any way
If it is dislocated from the toes or from under the muscle, and you see it with your eyes, do not be deceived.
And in this dislocation, the reduction is easy when it is fresh and the patient is young
And the reduction of it is that the minister raises the hand of the patient above the lower part; and he places the toes behind the tibia of the patient, and raises the joint strongly to the socket; the minister raises the hand of the patient and extends it out; and he pauses for a moment so that it returns willingly
Moreover, if despite what we have said it does not return, when it has happened from the beginning of the dislocation, moving days, cover that the patient should be bathed in lukewarm water and be administered embrocation that softens and soothes as if it were soothes radish of height, and fennel, and meadowsweet in water, and be administered
And thus the patient should be rested on the two thighs and be kept from moving from the tibia until the swelling has gone down between elevation and traction, and the physician should place his hand over the head of the muscle, that it is not swollen at the lower part, and another minister should hold the head of the patient, that it is not swollen at the lower part, for as much as that is necessary for the swelling to return to the socket
And if you wish, reduce it in this manner: make sure there is a man standing beside the patient who is taller than the patient, and let him put his hand under the knee of the patient and lift the knee up to the lower part of the thigh until the patient is suspended in the air, and another minister should pull the patient's hand away from the lower part of the thigh. And if the patient is groaning, cover him with something else, so that the dislocation will return immediately
And it is reduced immediately in another manner: and it is that a long staff is placed on the ground, the head of which is rounded like a mortar pestle, which is neither thick nor thin, and the patient is placed upon the head of the staff; since it is supported by the folds of the gown, the patient is standing according to the length of the staff, and the hand is extended outwards from the other side; and the body is stretched out from the other side with strength, so that the joint returns to the socket quickly
And if the reduction is difficult for all the causes that we have said, then use this treatment: take a staff as long as two palms and as wide as four fingers, and make the thickness of it broad enough to rest on the heel of the tibia in this way:
And thus rest on the rounded head put leather patches around it so that the staff does not damage the patient
And immediately suspend the patient's pulse, extend your hand or arm over the waist towards the lower parts, and tie the waist around the attendants and the arms and the hand.
Immediately suspend the arms on a support according to their width, and extend the hand towards the lower parts, and suspend the other limb from the other side, so that the joint is within.
And when the intestines are complete according to any way that you can, and when you have covered that you stop the pulse of the heel, prepare the powder of poppy and alum on all the muscles, even if it is twisted downwards, and strengthen the heel with a tight bandage; and the ligament is twisted on the dressing, and the hand is fixed to the chest, and is laid down, and do not move the hand for seven days
And cover that the patient should eat little food until the limb is comforted, because it is more likely to recover the health of the limb.
And the food should be given more often every seven or eight days or exercise a movement; and thus if it is stopped and is not softened, the hour has already healed
But if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has happened to it or for another cause, the hour covers that it should be cauterized with three incisions, as it is said in the chapter of cautery
And if all this has been done and seven days have passed, the ligament is loosened and the joint is not stopped, and the dressing and the bandage are reduced over it slightly, and it is not stopped and is cut and cannot raise that limb towards the upper parts, because the nerves of the limb, which are at the head of the muscle, are already insensible or extended or softened, and you know that the joint will never be fixed in place forever
From the dislocation of that which is useful for the feet and the heel or the lower parts, the reduction is useful with impulse and extension towards the greatest extent, until it returns
And it should be administered in the other way, and care for that until it is healed
And if it happens that the healing is slow in the limb and the movement of the limb is delayed, the hour of the patient uses lukewarm water until that gravity is relieved and returns to its natural state

Chapter XXVIII.
Of the care of dislocation of a limb, that is between the arm and the hand.
The dislocation of the hand frequently happens, and its reduction is easy, unlike that of the other joints, however it must be noted that the limb must not be too much displaced or that the dislocation happened with violent force.
And the reduction of the dislocation of the limb is to place the wrist of the patient over a table and extend the limb of that, and put your hand or palm over the area of the joint, and press that until it returns to its place
However it must be considered if the palm is already bowed towards the belly of the hand, then the patient must put two of his hands over a table at the time of extension and reduction; and if the dislocation is previous you must put two of the hand, then the position of the hand of the patient intrinsically over the table, so that the hand of the doctor covers that area of the joint
And thus if it returns quickly, well it is good; and if not, then you must stretch that over the paste giving up the apostema and leaving that; and do not repeat that, for if you do, you will suffer or will not be able to do the reduction any more than for several days
However the joint remains according to its stiffness; and do not note to the patient any cause, but that the hand is softened and cannot stretch any cause; for it is understood that the nerves are cut or crushed, and that it is not due to the limb itself but is stretched with a pointed cautery because of the position of the limb and the force which is conferred by the cause
Therefore when the limb is returned, then you rest over it the paste which we have recommended, and keep it stretched for five days; and then loosen it and keep it relaxed and exercise the hand
However if the movement of the limb is delayed and an accident happens in it any gravity, then you will gently massage that with cold water and do a few times with friction until it is relieved

Chapter XXV
Of the treatment of a dislocated ankle.
You must know that the ankle joint and the muscle joint do not suffer anything other than dislocation alone, and not from any other affections that affect the other joints of the little toe with swelling and concave depression
And the ankle joint is dislocated in four ways, which is either upwards, downwards, forwards or backwards
Mostly it is dislocated upwards, and slightly forwards or backwards
And a sign of the dislocation of the ankle is that, when you adjust the limb of the patient who is healed with the limb of the patient who is suffering, the limb of the patient who is suffering appears longer and the heel appears more prominent than the limb that is healed; the limb cannot bend its knee without causing pain, and the limb is bowed outwards as far as the heel has been moved forward by the cautery
The sign of the dislocation of the ankle is that it is in the opposite direction of this one
The sign of the dislocation of the ankle is that the limb expands slightly, but it does not bend where it is painful; if it is forced to bend, it cannot do so without causing pain; the urine is retained and the swelling is excessive, and you must walk the patient on the talus bone
The sign of the dislocation of the ankle is that the heel does not expand, nor can it bend downwards where it is painful; the limb is shorter than the other, the swelling is softened, and the heel has been moved forward from that place
More reduction of these species of dislocation is that you consider, when, if the dislocation is old and ancient, that it has already passed its best; in this case you must not do anything for it, for it is not necessary for treatment in this case; and indeed you must not attempt to do anything for it, for it will cause death to you
More in the case where the dislocation is recent, and is one of the four kinds of dislocation, then you must support the joint and extend it upwards and downwards, and to the right and left, for it is strong and does not require any other treatment
More so, if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong minister and extend the limb of the patient from the lower part, or from the middle or from the ligament which is bound over the limb below the ankle; and another minister should grasp the limb of the patient and support their toes; and strengthen the ligament with another minister over the back of the ankle and hold another minister over the foot.
And the extension of the limb from the heel to the ankle or from the heel to the ankle bone, or from the back to the tibia or from the back to the fibula.
And the extension of all these until the patient’s limb is elevated to the height of the knee and remains hanging down
And this kind of extension is common to all four kinds of dislocation
Therefore, if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is well; and if not, then treatment is necessary in all four cases.
In the reduction of the limb itself, when it is dislocated, and the dislocation is at the joints below, cover that the patient should rest upon the sitting bones; and immediately suspend the ligaments over the edge of the space in that place where between the head of the space and the place which is left to hang down; and extend the ligament from the part of the angulus to the highest part of the fork.
And immediately another minister should strengthen the patient's ankles, and measure the great space of the painful space and extend to the other side for violent extension, so that that which returned to the sitting place
And this kind of pus is lighter treatment than the one with which this limb is reduced than other kinds.
More if it is excused to you and you do not obey the order with this kind of treatment, however cover that the two feet of the patient be bound together with strong ligament, eagerly, over both ankles and both toes
And let the length of each by the quantity of four fingers, and let the painful limb be extended more than the other by the quantity of two fingers.
And immediately the patient should be suspended upon the head of the thigh, and that it be in the greater; and let the length of them from the earth be the quantity of two ankles.
And immediately command a a strong young man to shorten the head of the space, and that it be suspended with the patient another young man, and the other young man will shorten the limb with force pushing, so that the joint returns to the sitting place with speed.
However in the proper reduction, when the dislocation is at the outer part, cover that the patient follows his heel as we have recommended in the haven gelbozitat; and let the ligament be stretched over the painful limb itself and over the toes of it
And immediately two cushions are placed, one at the foot of the limb, and the other at the head; and cushions are placed adjusted to the middle of the limb which is left hanging over which damp cloth is wrapped, so that the patient is not moistened because the limb is between the patient's thighs, because you must extend to the other side not to be taut.
And immediately every minister extends their part, and the doctor with his hand grasps the reduction according to the art
And when the dislocation is at the ankle bones, it is necessary that the limb be extended eagerly, as it is according to this medical narration about the limb; and the doctor places the palm of his right hand over the painful ankle, and immediately grasp that with the other hand, and with that grasp pause that which was extended to the other side at the ankle bone
And if the dislocation is at the back parts, it is not necessary that the patient be extended to the toes, but it is elevated from the earth; because it is necessary that it be placed upon a hard cause, as if the ankle joint is dislocated to the outer parts, as we have said of the walking of the limb about two spans; and it is on its face and the ligaments are extended, as we have said, there is no spasm.
And it is necessary that cold compression be administered on the area where the joint is located.
Therefore when the reduction is completed as we have said — and the signal of the limb's reduction is not hidden from you, that you extend two cushions from the patient, and when you have once placed those cushions and the patient extends his limb the sitting limb and expands that excuse, then you know that the limb as we have said is returned — and immediately you adjust two cushions and place them close together and extend with a bandage so that the ankle is not swollen in any of the parts; and keep the patient at rest for three days or for four.
And immediately unbind the ligament and the bandage, and compare one limb with the other.
However, if you see those cushions in the bandage, you know that the dislocation is already stopped, and then you may allow the patient to leave.
And if you see any cause of discomfort, you know that you must return and place that one again, and extend that one according to your first structure, and leave that one for three days.
And immediately remove that one, and make that one walk slowly for some days, until it is comforted

From the care of dislocation of the toe.

Chapter XXXIII.</start_of_turn>
Of the care of dislocation of the ankle
The ankle is sometimes sprained by slight displacement, and sometimes it is dislocated according to custom, and the dislocation is caused either by excessive inward pressure or excessive outward pressure
And the sign of dislocation is that sometimes the ankle swells from the part which is dislocated
But the treatment of its displacement is of little relief, and that it should be easily extended with the greatest comfort and must be equal when it returns
But in the treatment of dislocation according to custom, cover that he does nothing but remove the hand which he has placed over the area, and take hold of that which is behind the two of those in the middle of the foot
And put your right hand on the great toe and your left hand on the lesser toe of the foot in the place of the ankle
And pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and with your left hand for two spans, and then extend with your left; and press the bones of the foot against the right side of the limb.
And do this for two spans as we have counted
And press the bones of the foot to the limb for the third span, and you are at the ankle
Therefore, if it returns in one span or two according to this manner, and if sometimes the foot is equaled, it is good; otherwise, repeat the operation until it returns
Moreover, if the reduction is prohibited to you in this case, then make the patient walk on the toes over the ground, and stretch a little on the ground, and keep him between the thighs, and you have already cauterized over him so that he does not burn himself
